<div id="review_1488668" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1488668" />
    <a title="Rhapsody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21602-rhapsody"><img alt="Rhapsody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1179613973p2/21602.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1488668?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rhapsody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rhapsody" href="/user/show/21602-rhapsody">Rhapsody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">romance/abused heroine fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21602-rhapsody?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21602-rhapsody?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21602-rhapsody?shelf=damsel-in-distress">damsel-in-distress</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1488668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15918120454574056032">One of my favorites by Anderson, and I've read a ton of her books. I've heard people complain that Annie's a little too innocent and simple and her relationship with Alex is more father-daughter than husband-wife, but I thought the story was lovely.<br/><br/>It's the late 1800's Oregon. Annie is the judge's youngest daughter and considered to be an imbecile. She had a fever when she was six that affected her brain, supposedly. At twenty, she's raped by Douglas Montgomery. The Montgomery family is very wea</span>
  <span id="freeText15918120454574056032" style="display:none">One of my favorites by Anderson, and I've read a ton of her books. I've heard people complain that Annie's a little too innocent and simple and her relationship with Alex is more father-daughter than husband-wife, but I thought the story was lovely.<br /><br />It's the late 1800's Oregon. Annie is the judge's youngest daughter and considered to be an imbecile. She had a fever when she was six that affected her brain, supposedly. At twenty, she's raped by Douglas Montgomery. The Montgomery family is very wealthy; Alex, the elder of the brothers, throws Douglas out of town. Annie's father decides not to prosecute because the stigma of having an idiot daughter might affect his chances in the political world. Alex, learning that Annie is pregnant four months after the rape, decides to marry her, figuring that he needs an heir and that it will be better for her. He had mumps as a child and believes himself to be sterile. As for Annie, he thinks she's retarded and doesn't think it would be cruel taking her child away from her and returning her to her parents after she's conceived. It doesn't take long for him to discover that she isn't an idiot, after which he starts falling in love with her and doing his best to win her heart.<br /><br />I guess I wouldn't recommend this to people who like the two mains to be very much equals who are always squaring off against each other. It isn't a battle-of-the-sexes story. It's already set in a patriarchal time, and Alex is somewhat older than Annie (eleven years maybe?), better-educated, richer, and not affected by a physical disability. He treats her very sweetly though and does his best to help her and make her happy once he understands the nature of her problem. Annie, who is quite intelligent, has been neglected, abused, and hidden away by her parents ever since she was six; she doesn't speak, can't read, write, or count, and is ignorant about a lot of stuff people would take for granted. However, the premise for her situation is totally believable. I hate subtle sexism in books, especially stupid heroines, and I can't stand romance novels where the male is so perfect and smart and the female gets jerked around by him constantly--this book wasn't like that at all. Also, Annie wasn't one of those horribly annoying heroines who is defined by her goodness and generosity and gentleness. She actually has depth and a personality and personal quirks.<br /><br />Anderson is such a good writer! Some of the scenes were so poignant. And the story had a timeless sense to it. Even though it was set in the past, it didn't have that faraway feel that some historical romance has. Other than how Annie is treated due to her disability, it pretty much feels like a contemporary setting.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15918120454574056032" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_104267510" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104267510" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277923282p2/3282244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104267510?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=rape-abuse">rape-abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=deaf-mute-blind-mad">deaf-mute-blind-mad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=it-moved-me">it-moved-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=excellent">excellent</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104267510" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7628696807870927420">Sometimes I look at the titles that are put on books and wonder why they're named that. Half the time they have nothing to do with the story at all. Here, the title actually has meaning. Annie is not what people think. No one has made the effort to discover the real her. It takes a special, though regrettable, set of circumstances and a special man to look past the stigma and listen closely enough to hear Annie's song.<br/><br/>The book starts out with a very disturbing event. Annie, the childlike town "i</span>
  <span id="freeText7628696807870927420" style="display:none">Sometimes I look at the titles that are put on books and wonder why they're named that. Half the time they have nothing to do with the story at all. Here, the title actually has meaning. Annie is not what people think. No one has made the effort to discover the real her. It takes a special, though regrettable, set of circumstances and a special man to look past the stigma and listen closely enough to hear Annie's song.<br /><br />The book starts out with a very disturbing event. Annie, the childlike town "idiot", is raped. The worst comes to pass and Annie becomes pregnant. Alex, the brother of the rapist, marries Annie to provide a home and name for the unborn child. He has no expectation of making the marriage a real one. He plans to go on with his life and expects Annie's nurse to keep her out of his way. Before long Alex find his view of Annie shaken. Soon he sees Annie in a new light and finds a love he never expected.<br /><br />This story was so beautiful. The people in it are not perfect and they don't always do the right thing. I hated some of them at times, but even then, they seemed like real people making real mistakes.<br /><br />Annie's mother comes off as a harsh, cruel woman. By the time Alex is getting to know the real Annie, you would be pleased if her mom would just die. You won't understand how a mother can treat her daughter like that. We, the reader, see the truth. Why is she denying it? It's frustrating and emotional, but eventually you learn to empathize with Annie's mother (even if you never really like her). That's what's so special about this story. There is no black and white. You find yourself wondering, "would I honestly have done such-and-such differently?" Then no matter what you feel, you can't help but admire her as she moves past her beliefs and tries to help her daughter live her new life.<br /><br />Alex was a hard man to read at first. He had a view of Annie and a feel of entitlement to her baby that was frightening at times. I'm glad that the things that bothered me the most: his plans for Annie after the baby was born, his contact with his brother, etc. were all discussed eventually with Annie. I thought that was very mature and even though I disliked him at times for his treatment of Annie in the beginning, I also recognize it as a very human reaction. From the moment when he asks her for that first dance I began to love him. The time and care he took with her and the determination to wait for her as long as it took... beautiful.<br /><br />Annie was an object of pity and heartbreak at times, but by the end of the book you'll realize that no matter her disability, she is the strongest character in the story. Through her life she put up with horrendous things and she still finds it in herself to love her family. She doesn't love blindly, she sees the faults and weaknesses in her parents and loves them despite them. Her love of her father is almost a mirror image of Alex's love of his brother. Through Annie you'll see the things you take for granted in a different light. She has a strong character and she knows what will make her life complete. Even though she knows what she wants, she's willing to bend to another character's view if she thinks it will make them happier.<br /><br />This was an awesome book and I strongly recommend it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7628696807870927420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Chryssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5527782-chryssa"><img alt="Chryssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453545052p2/5527782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a title="Chryssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chryssa" href="/user/show/5527782-chryssa">Chryssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chryssa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3201202-sophia">Sophia</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847348632" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12091989492199226551"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392278017i/8531407._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>The story</u>
</b><br/>Annie Trimble is considered the town's simpleton, <b>Annie the dummy</b>, whom everyone makes fun of but does not harm, most of the times. Until Douglas Montgomery, your usual rich spoilt man, the town's bully, sets his eyes on her and rapes her...for fun. Alex Mongtgomery, his older brother tries to make amends by marrying Annie and providing for the child resulting from her rape. What has started as so dreadful blossoms to a great love story against all the hero's expectations.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Annie</u>
</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392276176i/8531097.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>L</span>
  <span id="freeText12091989492199226551" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392278017i/8531407._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>The story</u>
</b><br>Annie Trimble is considered the town's simpleton, <b>Annie the dummy</b>, whom everyone makes fun of but does not harm, most of the times. Until Douglas Montgomery, your usual rich spoilt man, the town's bully, sets his eyes on her and rapes her...for fun. Alex Mongtgomery, his older brother tries to make amends by marrying Annie and providing for the child resulting from her rape. What has started as so dreadful blossoms to a great love story against all the hero's expectations.<br><br><b>
  <u>Annie</u>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392276176i/8531097.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Lost in her silence, she lives in a world of her own where every desire of hers become alive in her make-believe, considered childish by all, games. Abused, not only by the obvious perperator but also by the ones she loves the most, her parents. Annie comes always in second place after her father's political aspirations and her mother's fear of her husband's divorcing her. The greatest instances of family abuse happen "in the name of love" and "because the neighbors must not know" and Annie is a living example of this.<br><br><b>
  <u>Alex</u>
</b><br>Honorable, decent, kindhearted, not a saint in any case and that's what makes him real. A hot-blooded man, admitting to his desires and pursuing them without any fear, he wins the reader with his consistency and persistence. Though a fallible man, he tries to do what's best for Annie even at the expense of his happiness. Besides his love, he wants to give her whatever was taken from her, even when this may lead to losing her forever.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392276593i/8531139.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>...♫And I try, oh my God, do I try I try all the time♫...</u>
</b><br>For readers that adore heroes and heroines with deficits, stories with intense emotions, the description of this book was the proverbial honey (preferable to carrots!)...but <u>I coudn't, hard as I tried, find this angst I sought</u>. It was a sweet story, beautifully written and developped, my first - but not my last!- Catherine Anderson book. Despite my trying so very hard to adore it, some scenes IMO did not add to the story and were totally unnecessary, even when the author explains why she wrote them as such <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a very 9.5 Weeks scene, including some ice cream and the oh so innocent/afraid of love-making and any kind of intimacy heroine...purring (!) <i>"I want to be your ice cream"</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, thus making me snatch a star from the rating at 86% of the book. I admit that the last 2 Chapters indeed gave an added interest and peaked the story, in all fairness ending the book wonderfully!<br><b>Certainly precious reading time worth spent.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392286403i/8532770._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Annie and Alex found that place dancing the silent waltz to Annie's song.<br><br><br><i>*Pictures and quote by James Leeds taken from a wonderful film, topic related, though set a century later than the book <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0090830/" rel="nofollow noopener">Children of a Lesser God (1986)</a></i><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="12091989492199226551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/917649459?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/17984545-annie-s-song">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=gentle-hero">gentle-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=guys-i-want">guys-i-want</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=strong-heroines">strong-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19387048-chumchum-88?shelf=shy-heroines">shy-heroines</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer917649459" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2311733314960585862">I just finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/659600.Annie_s_Song' title='Annie's Song by Catherine Anderson' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1325836635s/659600.jpg' alt='Annie's Song by Catherine Anderson' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a>and I'd like to say its Phenomenal!!! its seriously amazing.<br/>For one thing I really loved the book so I'm starting to get interested in the author.<br/>and another thing that there wasn't a single thing in the book that I hated, maybe except all the misunderstanding that's happening, starting from her fear of him even after months she still feared him, but its understandable since she's deaf and neglected.<br/>nearing the end I was this close to tears, I tried my best to hold the tears </span>
  <span id="freeText2311733314960585862" style="display:none">I just finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/659600.Annie_s_Song" title="Annie's Song by Catherine Anderson" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1325836635s/659600.jpg" alt="Annie's Song by Catherine Anderson" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a>and I'd like to say its Phenomenal!!! its seriously amazing.<br>For one thing I really loved the book so I'm starting to get interested in the author.<br>and another thing that there wasn't a single thing in the book that I hated, maybe except all the misunderstanding that's happening, starting from her fear of him even after months she still feared him, but its understandable since she's deaf and neglected.<br>nearing the end I was this close to tears, I tried my best to hold the tears back cause I was in public, but if I wasn't I know I would have cried floods, cause the ending is That emotional.<br>the main characters were the most adorable especially the main guy, cause he was heart wrenchingly kind, and how patient and sweet he was with her, and when he showered her with his love with the gifts how happy he looked to me from the books, because the writer described his behavior and his as if I really can see him, and I just have to say that hes now one of my favorite male characters ever, so for me its a *thumps up*</span>
  <a data-text-id="2311733314960585862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KSf5yTmWDcmh4oPkbBqLm4cO/wMzBJ9KbR+S164Wh0CnWkXNj60MHYHvi3wsuaeVlkr79eHAnL+2iozwiamYjw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('x0fTgtkP2M0YW6rdHTofXJVRxdDb3reiyeFA9wytFuJJOm+GbzTZGThWokVdmTNShBXBJgkatFcSdF7QKxIJLQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/51304.Catherine_Anderson">About Catherine Anderson</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/51304.Catherine_Anderson"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1231741566p3/51304.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/51304.Catherine_Anderson">Catherine Anderson
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
2,406
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2772628075870121584"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces' rel='nofollow noopener'>See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br/>(1)romance author:<br/>Adeline Catherine was born and raised in Grants Pass, Oregon, USA. She always yearned to be a writer like her mother. The morning that one of her professors asked if she could use samples of Catherine’s creative writing on an overhead projector to teach was</span>
  <span id="freeText2772628075870121584" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the GoodReads database with this name. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show_group/44217.Master_List_of_Author_Disambiguation_by_Spaces" rel="nofollow noopener">See this thread for more information</a>.</i><br />(1)romance author:<br />Adeline Catherine was born and raised in Grants Pass, Oregon, USA. She always yearned to be a writer like her mother. The morning that one of her professors asked if she could use samples of Catherine’s creative writing on an overhead projector to teach was a dream come true. In 1988, she sold her first book to Harlequin Intrigue and went on to write three more before she tried her hand at a single-title historical romance. Nine books later, she did her first single-title contemporary.<br /><br />Catherine married Sidney D. Anderson, an industrial electrician and entrepreneur. They had two sons, Sidney D. Jr. and John G. In 2001 she and her husband purchased a central Oregon home located on a ridge with incredible mountain views and surrounded by forestland honeycombed with trails. It was her dream home, a wonderland in the winter and beyond beautiful in the summer. She named it Cinnamon Ridge after the huge ponderosa pines on the property, which sport bark the color of cinnamon.<br /><br />Sadly, Catherine lost her husband to a long-term illness in 2014. She has kept Cinnamon Ridge as her primary residence but divides her time between there and her son John's farm, where she has the support of her loved ones and can enjoy his horses, cows, and raise her own chickens.<br /><br />Catherine loves animals and birds, both wild and domestic. She presently has two Australian shepherds, six cats, and a very old canary. She is very family oriented as well. Her older son has lived in Japan, Australia, and now resides in New Zealand. Catherine and her stateside family will celebrate Christmas on the north island with Sidney, his wife Mary, and their two sons, Liam and Jonas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2772628075870121584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/645677-annie-s-song">Quotes from Annie&#39;s Song</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;Annie giggled again. She couldn’t seem to stop herself. And when she did, the most incredible thing happened. Alex’s grin vanished, and after gazing down at her for what seemed to her several endless seconds, he got tears in his eyes. “Thank you,” he said. Only that, just a simple “thank you.” But to Annie, those were the two most wonderful words she’d ever seen spoken, and they meant more to her than a thousand others might have. With them, he told her a wealth of things, namely that he had meant everything he’d said to her in the attic, that he not only wouldn’t punish her for making noise, but that he wanted her to.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
